وقوله : (مُعَذَّبٌ مُنَعَمٌ ) أي : فداخل النار مُعذَّبٌ فيها بأنواع العذاب : كالزمهرير والحيات والعقارب وغير ذلك. وداخل الجنة مُنعم فيها بأنواع النعيم : وأعلاه رؤية وجه الله الكريم. وقوله : (مَهْمَا بَقِي) أي مدة بقاء كل من الفريقين في إحدى الدارين . وما يُقال : يتمرن أهل النار بالعذاب، حتى لو ألقوا فى الجنة لتألموا .. مدسوس على القوم. كيف وقد قال تعالى: ﴿فَذُوقُوا فَلَن نَّزِيدَكُمْ إِلَّا عَذَابًا﴾ [النبا : ٣٠]
And his saying: (punished, blissful) means: the one entering the Fire is punished therein with types of punishment: like the extreme cold, snakes, scorpions, and others. And the one entering Paradise is blissful therein with types of bliss: its highest is the vision of the generous face of Allah. And his saying: (as long as they remain) means the duration of the stay of each of the two groups in one of the two abodes. And what is said: that the people of the Fire are trained by punishment, such that if they were thrown into Paradise they would feel pain — it is an intrusion upon the people. How? While Allah the Exalted has said: 'So taste, and We will not increase you except in punishment' [An-Naba: 30].
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of two phrases from the poem: 'مُعَذَّبٌ مُنَعَمٌ' and 'مَهْمَا بَقِي'. The commentator first clarifies that 'punished' refers to those in Hell who suffer various types of punishment including intense cold (zamharir), snakes, scorpions, and other torments. 'Blissful' refers to those in Paradise who enjoy various types of bliss, the highest of which is the vision of Allah's gracious face — a central tenet of Sunni belief. Then he explains 'مهما بقي' as the duration of the stay of each group in their respective abode, implying eternity. He then refutes a claim that the people of Hell become habituated to punishment to the point that they would feel pain if cast into Paradise. He dismisses this idea as 'مدسوس' (an intrusion or forgery) upon the people, backing his refutation with the Qur'anic verse 'فذوقوا فلن نزيدكم إلا عذابا' — which states that their punishment will only increase, not decrease or become tolerable.

مدسوس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Hell's inhabitants become so accustomed to punishment that they would feel pain if placed in Paradise.
Correction: The commentator refutes this, stating it is an intrusion, and cites the Qur'anic verse indicating that punishment only increases, not diminishes.

B) Gardens and rivers

Key Takeaway
Eternal punishment is ever-increasing, and eternal bliss culminates in seeing Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The highest bliss in Paradise is seeing Allah's face. Is this actually your greatest desire, or have you been more preoccupied with lesser pleasures? What would it take for this longing to become the driving force of your life?
?
The claim that Hell's inhabitants become accustomed to punishment is dismissed as a forgery. But in your own heart, have you ever quietly hoped that maybe, just maybe, the punishment won't be so bad? How does this verse confront that hope, and what should your response be right now?

State of People on the Day of Judgment
A benefit on the state of people in the standing-place and the bodies of believers and disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical states of believers and disbelievers on the Day of Judgment as described in this passage.

Core Idea
Believers enter Paradise in perfect youth; disbelievers suffer bodies of monstrous size.

This passage shares a prophetic report about the resurrection. It tells us that people remain as they died until judgment, then believers receive ideal bodies while disbelievers' bodies become enormous as a sign of punishment. Let's explore these details.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text carefully, then the English translation. Notice the specific measurements and the names of mountains.
The passage is a 'benefit' (fāʼidah), summarizing hadith.
2
Identify the states of believers
The passage describes believers entering Paradise naked, hairless, at age 33, with fixed dimensions. Reflect on why these details are given.
These are based on authentic hadith.
3
Understand the disbelievers' bodies
The disbelievers' bodies vary, but the text gives extreme examples: molar like Uhud, thigh like Wariqan. What does this convey about their punishment?
The mountains are in Medina.
4
Connect to broader eschatology
Consider how this passage fits with the overall Islamic understanding of bodily resurrection and the afterlife.
This is a glimpse into the physical realities of the Hereafter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة : الناسُ يكونون في الموقف على حالتهم التي ماتوا عليها، ثم يدخل المؤمنون الجنة جُرْداً مُرْداً أبناء ثلاث وثلاثين سنةً، طول كلِّ واحدٍ منهم ستون ذراعاً ، وعرضه سبعة أذرع ، ثم لا يزيدون ولا ينقصون. وأما أجسام الكفار فمختلفة المقادير ، حتى ورد أن ضِرْسَ الكافر في النار مثل أُحُدٍ ، وفخذه مثل وَرِقَان؛ وهما جبلان بالمدينة، كما في شرح.
A benefit: people will be in the standing-place upon the state they died upon. Then the believers enter Paradise naked, hairless, as young men of thirty-three years, the length of each of them sixty cubits, and his width seven cubits, then they neither increase nor decrease. As for the bodies of the disbelievers, they vary in sizes, even it is reported that the molar of the disbeliever in the Fire is like Mount Uhud, and his thigh like Wariqan — they are two mountains in Medina, as in the commentary.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a 'fāʼidah' (benefit) that summarizes a prophetic report about the physical state of people on the Day of Judgment. It states that people remain in the station of resurrection (al-mawqif) in the same condition they died—implying that their deeds, beliefs, and physical states are preserved. Then the believers enter Paradise 'jurdan murdan' (hairless, beardless) at the age of thirty-three, with a height of sixty cubits and a width of seven cubits, and these dimensions are fixed—they do not change. This is based on authentic hadith. In contrast, the bodies of disbelievers are not uniform; they vary greatly. The text gives examples from tradition: a disbeliever's molar is as large as Mount Uhud, and his thigh is as large as Mount Wariqan (two well-known mountains near Medina). This underscores the grandeur and horror of the punishment.

Misconception: Some might think that people are resurrected in the same physical age and size they had in this world.
Correction: The hadith specifies that believers enter Paradise at a specific young age and size (33 years, 60 cubits tall) that remain unchanged thereafter.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The disbeliever's punishment includes a molar the size of a mountain. Have you ever dismissed a 'small' sin as insignificant? How does this literal, physical magnification of punishment challenge your view of the gravity of your own actions—and what will you do differently starting now?

Belief in the Prophet's Basin (Hawd): Obligation and Description
Commentator defines the Hawd, declares belief obligatory, refutes Mu'tazila, and describes it with hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation of believing in the Prophet's Basin (Hawd), the ruling on denying it, its physical description from authentic hadith, and why the Mu'tazila's rejection is refuted.

Core Idea
Belief in the Prophet's Basin is obligatory; denial is a sin, not disbelief.

The commentator begins by affirming that belief in the Prophet's Basin is an obligatory matter based on transmitted reports. He clarifies that while belief is mandatory, denying it does not expel one from Islam but makes one a sinner. This passage also provides a vivid description of the Hawd from authentic hadith and refutes the Mu'tazila who rejected it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on belief in the Hawd
Read the commentary's opening where it explains that belief is obligatory (wājib) and that denial is fisq, not kufr. Note the contrast with the Mu'tazila position.
2
Explore the physical description of the Hawd
Examine the description of the Hawd as a huge body on the substituted earth, with whiter-than-milk water, better-than-musk smell, and more cups than stars. Understand that it is for this ummah.
The description comes from hadith in the Two Sahihs.
3
Learn the proof from tawātur
Notice that the commentator highlights that the hadith about the Prophet's Basin have reached the level of tawātur (mass transmission), unlike the Basins of other prophets which are from āḥād reports.
This strengthens the obligation of belief.
4
Reflect on the refutation of the Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila denied the Hawd. The commentator shows the author refutes them by presenting the evidence. Consider why their denial is considered sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوبُ الإيمان بحوض النبي ]
١١١ - إِيْمَانُنا بِحَوْضِ خَيْرِ الرُّسُلِ حَتْمٌ كَمَا قَدْ جَاءَنَا فِي النَّقْل
قوله : (إِيْمَانُنا بِحَوْضِ خَيْرِ الرُّسُلِ حَنْمٌ أي : تصديقنا بالحوض الذي يعطاه في الآخرة أفضل المرسلين؛ وهو نبينا محمد و واجب ، لكن لا يكفر من أنكره، وإنما يفسق، وقد نفته المعتزلة، ولذلك أشار المصنف للردّ عليهم بما ذكر .
السمعيات وهي [؟] وهو جسم مخصوص كبير متسعُ الجوانب يكون على الأرض المُبدَّلة ؛ الأرض البيضاء كالفِضَّة، مَنْ شرب منه لا يظمأ أبداً، تَرِدُهُ هذه الأمة، وقد ورد أن لكل نبي حوضاً تردُّه أمته، فعن الحسن مرفوعاً : إن لكل نبي حوضاً، وهو قائم على حوضه وبيده عصاً يدعو مَنْ عرف من أمته ألا وإنهم يتباهون أيهم أكثر تبعاً، وإني لأرجو أن أكون أكثرهم تبعاً .
وفي أثر : أن حوضه أعرضُ الحيضان وأكثرها وارداً، وتخصيص حوض نبينا
بالذكر ؛ لوروده بالأحاديث البالغة مبلغ التواتر، بخلاف غيره؛ لوروده بالآحاد. وقوله : كَمَا قَدْ جَاءَنَا فِي النَّقْلِ ) أي : للنص الذي قد ورد إلينا في المنقول عنه ؛ ففي الصحيحين من حديث عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص رضي الله عنهما : حوضي مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيضُ من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء، مَنْ شرب منه فلا يظمأ أبداً، وقد ورد تحديده بجهاتٍ مختلفة، ففي روايةٍ لأحمد: إن الحوض كما بين عَدَن وعُمان، وذلك نحو شهر.
The obligation of belief in the Prophet's Basin
111 - Our belief in the Basin of the best of messengers is absolutely binding as has come to us in transmitted report.
His saying: (Our belief in the Basin of the best of messengers is binding) means: our affirmation of the Basin which will be given in the Hereafter to the best of messengers, and he is our Prophet Muhammad, is obligatory, but one who denies it does not become a disbeliever, rather he becomes a sinner. The Mu'tazila have denied it, and therefore the author pointed to refuting them by what he mentioned.
The auditory matters: and it is [?] and it is a specific huge body with wide sides, located on the substituted earth — the white earth like silver. Whoever drinks from it never thirsts. This ummah will come to it. It has been reported that every prophet has a Basin that his ummah will come to. From al-Hasan in marfu' form: 'Indeed every prophet has a Basin, and he stands at his Basin with a staff in his hand, calling those he knows from his ummah. Verily they boast of who has more followers, and I hope to be the one with the most followers.'
And in an athar: that his Basin is the widest of basins and the most frequented. And the specification of our Prophet's Basin by mention is because it is reported by hadith that have reached the level of tawatur, unlike others which are reported by ahad hadith. And his saying: (as has come to us in transmitted report) means: the text that has reached us in what is transmitted. For in the Two Sahihs from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, may Allah be pleased with both of them: 'My Basin is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its smell is better than musk, its cups are more than the stars of the sky. Whoever drinks from it never thirsts ever.' And its measurement has been reported with different dimensions. In a narration by Ahmad: 'The Basin is like between Aden and Oman' — that is about a month.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the Hawd (Basin) of the Prophet. It begins with the line from the poem 'إيماننا بحوض خير الرسل حتم' and its commentary. The commentator explains that 'belief in the Hawd' means affirming the existence of the special Basin that the Prophet will be given in the afterlife. He clarifies that belief in it is obligatory (wājib), but denying it does not necessitate apostasy (takfir); rather, it is a sin (fisq). The Mu'tazila rejected this, so the author hints at refuting them. The text then transitions into a physical description of the Hawd under the heading of sam'iyyāt (auditory matters). It describes the Hawd as a huge, wide-sided body located on the 'substituted earth' (al-arḍ al-mubaddala) — a white earth like silver. Whoever drinks from it will never thirst again. It is for this ummah to come to. The passage also notes that every prophet has a Basin for his own ummah, citing a marfu' narration from al-Hasan that the prophets stand by their Basins and call their followers, boasting about numbers. The Prophet's Basin is singled out because its hadith have reached tawātur (widespread multiple chains), unlike others which are āḥād (solitary). The passage then provides a detailed hadith from the Two Sahihs — the famous description: a month's journey, whiter than milk, smell better than musk, cups more than stars, and eternal quench. Another narration from Ahmad compares it to the distance between Aden and Oman, also about a month's journey.

معتزلة
فسق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying the Prophet's Basin (Hawd) is an act of disbelief (kufr).
Correction: The commentator states explicitly that one who denies it does not become a disbeliever, but rather becomes a sinner (fāsiq). Denial is sinful but not apostasy.

Checkpoint

A) He becomes a disbeliever
B) He becomes a sinner but not a disbeliever
C) He is considered a hypocrite
D) He must be killed for apostasy

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Prophet's Basin is obligatory based on mutawatir hadith, but denial is a sin, not disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Mu'tazila denied the Hawd because it did not fit their rational framework. Where in your own life do you find yourself valuing your intellect over the clear words of Revelation? Will you repent from that pride today?
?
The Prophet said he will stand at his Basin with a staff, calling those he knows from his ummah. Imagine that moment. Will he recognize you? What are you doing right now to ensure that he will?

The Reality and Authority of the Prophet's Ḥawḍ
Definition of the Ḥawḍ and authentication via tawātur, followed by the main hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the Prophet's Ḥawḍ and why its description is considered authoritative (tawātur) in contrast to other prophetic ḥawḍs.

Core Idea
The Prophet's Ḥawḍ is a real, massive cistern known through mass-transmitted hadiths.

The commentator begins by explaining one of the samʿiyyāt matters—the Ḥawḍ of the Prophet. This passage defines what the Ḥawḍ is, establishes that every prophet has one, and highlights that our Prophet's Ḥawḍ is specifically emphasized because its reports have reached the level of tawātur. You will then read the famous hadith describing its dimensions and qualities.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of the Ḥawḍ
Notice that the commentator describes the Ḥawḍ as a specific large body of water on the transformed earth, with the property that whoever drinks from it will never thirst.
Also note that it is for this specific nation (ummah).
2
Understand the authentication argument
The commentator states that every prophet has a Ḥawḍ, but the Prophet Muḥammad's is mentioned because it is transmitted via tawātur, whereas others are via āḥād reports. This establishes the reliability of the description.
3
Examine the primary hadith
Read the hadith from the two Ṣaḥīḥs via ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAmr. This hadith provides key details: a month's journey, white water, sweet smell, and numerous jugs.
This hadith is the foundation for the Ḥawḍ's description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات
وهي
وهو جسم مخصوص كبير متسعُ الجوانب يكون على الأرض المُبدَّلة ؛ الأرض البيضاء كالفِضَّة، مَنْ شرب منه لا يظمأ أبداً، تَرِدُهُ هذه الأمة، وقد ورد أن لكل نبي حوضاً تردُّه أمته، فعن الحسن مرفوعاً : إن لكل نبي حوضاً، وهو قائم على حوضه وبيده عصاً يدعو مَنْ عرف من أمته ألا وإنهم يتباهون أيهم أكثر تبعاً، وإني لأرجو أن أكون أكثرهم تبعاً » .
وفي أثر : أن حوضه أعرضُ الحيضان وأكثرها وارداً، وتخصيص حوض نبينا بالذكر ؛ لوروده بالأحاديث البالغة مبلغ التواتر، بخلاف غيره؛ لوروده بالآحاد. وقوله : كَمَا قَدْ جَاءَنَا فِي النَّقْلِ ) أي : للنص الذي قد ورد إلينا في المنقول عنه ؛ ففي الصحيحين من حديث عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص رضي الله عنهما : حوضي مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيضُ من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء، مَنْ شرب منه فلا يظمأ أبداً» ، وقد ورد تحديده بجهاتٍ مختلفة، ففي روايةٍ لأحمد: إن الحوض كما بين عَدَن وعُمان» ، وذلك نحو شهر. وقد روى في رواية «الصحيحين»: «ما بين صنعاء والمدينة، وذلك نحو شهرين. وفي رواية : ما بين مكةَ وأَيْلَة ، وذلك نحو شهر وفي رواية لابن ماجه : ما بين المدينة إلى بيت المقدس ، وهو كالذي قبله فقد تحدَّث المصطفى بحديث الحوض مرات، وذكر فيها تلك الألفاظ المختلفة، فكان يُخاطب كل قوم بالجهة التي يعرفونها، ولا تنافي من حيث تقدير المسافة بنحو شهر في بعض الروايات وبنحو شهرين في بعض آخر ؛ لأنَّ الله سبحانه وتعالى تفضّل عليه باتساعه شيئاً فشيئاً، فأخبر بالمسافة القصيرة أولاً، ثم أخبر بالمسافة الطويلة، والاعتماد على ما يدل على أطولها مسافة، كما أشار إليه النووي، وفيما أوحى الله تعالى إلى عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام من صفة نبينا : له حوض أبعد من مكة إلى مطلع الشمس فيه آنيةٌ مثلُ عدد نجوم السماء، وله لونُ كلِّ شراب الجنة وطعم كل ثمارها، وقوله في هذه الرواية مثل عدد نجوم السماء»، لا ينافي قوله : في الرواية السابقة: «أكثر من نجوم السماء»؛ لاحتمال أنه أخبر أولاً بأنها مثل ثم أخبر ثانياً بأنها أكثر، ومعنى كونه له لون كل شراب الجنة : أن بعضَه لونه أحمر، وبعضه لونه أبيض وهكذا، فلا يرد أن فيه الجمع بين الأضداد، وهو ممتنع، ومعنى كونه له طعم كل ثمارها : أن له طعم الخوخ والموز والمشمش وغيرها فمن يشرب منه يجد طعم ثمار الجنة .
The samʿiyyāt (matters heard from revelation). And it (the ḥawḍ) is a specific large body having wide sides, located upon the transformed earth (the white earth like silver). Whoever drinks from it will never thirst. This nation will come to it. And it has been reported that every prophet has a ḥawḍ which his nation comes to. From al-Ḥasan, raised (marfūʿ): 'Indeed, every prophet has a ḥawḍ, and he stands at his ḥawḍ with a staff in his hand calling those he knows from his nation. Lo! they boast as to which of them has more followers, and I hope to be the one with the most followers.' And in an athar (report): that his ḥawḍ is the widest of ḥawḍs and the most frequented. And the specification of our Prophet's ḥawḍ for mention is because it came in aḥādīth reaching the level of tawātur (mass transmission), unlike others which came in āḥād (solitary) reports. And his statement: 'as has come to us in transmission' means: the text that has reached us from that which is transmitted. For in the two Ṣaḥīḥs, from the ḥadīth of ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAmr ibn al-ʿĀṣ (may Allah be pleased with them both): 'My ḥawḍ is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its smell is sweeter than musk, its jugs are more numerous than the stars of the sky. Whoever drinks from it will never thirst.' And it has been reported with different estimates of directions. In a narration of Aḥmad: 'Indeed, the ḥawḍ is as between ʿAdan and ʿUmān' – that is about a month. And in a narration of the two Ṣaḥīḥs: '(It is) between Ṣanʿā' and al-Madīnah' – that is about two months. And in a narration: 'between Makkah and Aylah' – that is about a month. And in a narration of Ibn Mājah: 'between al-Madīnah and Bayt al-Maqdis' – which is like the previous one. So the Muṣṭafā (the Chosen One) spoke about the ḥadīth of the ḥawḍ multiple times and mentioned those different expressions. He addressed each group according to the direction they knew. And there is no contradiction in terms of estimating the distance as about a month in some narrations and about two months in others, because Allah (Exalted and High) favored him by enlarging it little by little. So he informed of the short distance first, then informed of the long distance. And reliance is on that which indicates the longest distance, as al-Nawawī indicated. And in what Allah revealed to ʿĪsā (peace be upon him) as a description of our Prophet: 'He has a ḥawḍ further than from Makkah to the rising place of the sun, in it are vessels like the number of the stars of the sky, and it has the color of every drink of Paradise and the taste of every fruit of Paradise.' And his statement in this narration 'like the number of the stars of the sky' does not contradict his statement in the previous narration 'more than the stars of the sky' because it is possible that he first informed that it is like, then secondly informed that it is more. And the meaning of 'it has the color of every drink of Paradise' is that some of it is red, some of it is white, and so on. Thus it is not objected that it involves the combination of opposites, which is impossible. And the meaning of 'it has the taste of every fruit of Paradise' is that it has the taste of peach, banana, apricot, and others. So whoever drinks from it finds the taste of the fruits of Paradise.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the Prophet's Ḥawḍ (Cistern), a matter of samʿiyyāt (revealed knowledge). The commentator begins by defining it as a large body of water with wide sides, located on the transformed earth (the white earth like silver), and whoever drinks from it will never thirst. It is specifically for this nation, though every prophet has a ḥawḍ for his own nation, as supported by a marfūʿ ḥadīth from al-Ḥasan. The commentator highlights that our Prophet's ḥawḍ is singled out for mention because its descriptions have reached the level of tawātur (mass transmission), unlike those of other prophets which are based on āḥād (solitary) reports. The phrase 'as has come to us in transmission' refers to authoritative texts. The commentator then cites the famous ḥadīth from the two Ṣaḥīḥs via ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAmr, describing the ḥawḍ as a month's journey, with water whiter than milk, sweeter than musk, and jugs more numerous than stars. He notes that different narrations give varying distances (e.g., as between ʿAdan and ʿUmān, between Ṣanʿāʾ and al-Madīnah, between Makkah and Aylah, between al-Madīnah and Bayt al-Maqdis). The commentator reconciles these differences by explaining that the Prophet addressed each audience according to the direction they knew, and that Allah gradually enlarged the ḥawḍ, so the shorter distance was mentioned first and the longer later. The reliance is on the longest distance, as al-Nawawī indicated. Further, he mentions a revelation to ʿĪsā describing the ḥawḍ as extending from Makkah to the sunrise, with vessels like stars. The commentator reconciles the wording 'like' versus 'more than' the stars as successive reports, not contradictions. He also explains that the ḥawḍ having the color of every drink and taste of every fruit of Paradise means its parts have different colors and tastes, not that a single drink combines opposites, which is impossible.

Key Terms
السمعيات (al-samʿiyyāt)
الحوض (al-ḥawḍ)
الأرض المبدلة (al-arḍ al-mubaddala)
التواتر (al-tawātur)
الآحاد (al-āḥād)

C) Because it is the only Ḥawḍ that exists.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's Ḥawḍ is a confirmed reality with a detailed description, authenticated by mass-transmitted hadiths.

Reconciling Variations in Ḥawḍ Descriptions
Reconciliation of various hadith reports on the Ḥawḍ's distance and description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the method for reconciling the different distances and descriptions of the Ḥawḍ found in various hadiths.

Core Idea
Apparent contradictions in Ḥawḍ narrations are resolved by noting different audiences and gradual enlargement.

The commentator now addresses the differences in the reported distances of the Ḥawḍ. He lists several narrations with varying distances (e.g., a month, two months) and offers a reconciliation: the Prophet addressed each audience according to the direction they knew, and Allah progressively enlarged the Ḥawḍ. He also resolves a seeming discrepancy between 'like number of stars' and 'more than stars', and explains the meaning of the Ḥawḍ having the color of every drink and taste of every fruit.

Guided Path
1
List the different distances
Read the four narrations cited: between ʿAdan and ʿUmān, between Ṣanʿāʾ and Madīnah, between Makkah and Aylah, between Madīnah and Bayt al-Maqdis. Note the estimated travel times.
One narration gives a month, another two months.
2
Understand the first reconciliation method
The commentator explains that the Prophet spoke multiple times, addressing each group by the distance they knew. Also, Allah gradually enlarged the Ḥawḍ, so the shorter distance was reported first.
This removes contradiction because the reports describe different stages or different audiences.
3
Reconcile 'like' vs 'more than' stars
The commentator says that the Prophet first said 'like' and later 'more than' due to successive reports, not contradiction.
4
Understand the colors and tastes explanation
The commentator clarifies that the Ḥawḍ having the color of every drink means different parts have different colors, not a single drink with multiple colors. Similarly, it has the taste of every fruit.
This avoids the notion of combining opposites.

السمعيات
وهي
وهو جسم مخصوص كبير متسعُ الجوانب يكون على الأرض المُبدَّلة ؛ الأرض البيضاء كالفِضَّة، مَنْ شرب منه لا يظمأ أبداً، تَرِدُهُ هذه الأمة، وقد ورد أن لكل نبي حوضاً تردُّه أمته، فعن الحسن مرفوعاً : إن لكل نبي حوضاً، وهو قائم على حوضه وبيده عصاً يدعو مَنْ عرف من أمته ألا وإنهم يتباهون أيهم أكثر تبعاً، وإني لأرجو أن أكون أكثرهم تبعاً » .
وفي أثر : أن حوضه أعرضُ الحيضان وأكثرها وارداً، وتخصيص حوض نبينا بالذكر ؛ لوروده بالأحاديث البالغة مبلغ التواتر، بخلاف غيره؛ لوروده بالآحاد. وقوله : كَمَا قَدْ جَاءَنَا فِي النَّقْلِ ) أي : للنص الذي قد ورد إلينا في المنقول عنه ؛ ففي الصحيحين من حديث عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص رضي الله عنهما : حوضي مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيضُ من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء، مَنْ شرب منه فلا يظمأ أبداً» ، وقد ورد تحديده بجهاتٍ مختلفة، ففي روايةٍ لأحمد: إن الحوض كما بين عَدَن وعُمان» ، وذلك نحو شهر. وقد روى في رواية «الصحيحين»: «ما بين صنعاء والمدينة، وذلك نحو شهرين. وفي رواية : ما بين مكةَ وأَيْلَة ، وذلك نحو شهر وفي رواية لابن ماجه : ما بين المدينة إلى بيت المقدس ، وهو كالذي قبله فقد تحدَّث المصطفى بحديث الحوض مرات، وذكر فيها تلك الألفاظ المختلفة، فكان يُخاطب كل قوم بالجهة التي يعرفونها، ولا تنافي من حيث تقدير المسافة بنحو شهر في بعض الروايات وبنحو شهرين في بعض آخر ؛ لأنَّ الله سبحانه وتعالى تفضّل عليه باتساعه شيئاً فشيئاً، فأخبر بالمسافة القصيرة أولاً، ثم أخبر بالمسافة الطويلة، والاعتماد على ما يدل على أطولها مسافة، كما أشار إليه النووي، وفيما أوحى الله تعالى إلى عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام من صفة نبينا : له حوض أبعد من مكة إلى مطلع الشمس فيه آنيةٌ مثلُ عدد نجوم السماء، وله لونُ كلِّ شراب الجنة وطعم كل ثمارها، وقوله في هذه الرواية مثل عدد نجوم السماء»، لا ينافي قوله : في الرواية السابقة: «أكثر من نجوم السماء»؛ لاحتمال أنه أخبر أولاً بأنها مثل ثم أخبر ثانياً بأنها أكثر، ومعنى كونه له لون كل شراب الجنة : أن بعضَه لونه أحمر، وبعضه لونه أبيض وهكذا، فلا يرد أن فيه الجمع بين الأضداد، وهو ممتنع، ومعنى كونه له طعم كل ثمارها : أن له طعم الخوخ والموز والمشمش وغيرها فمن يشرب منه يجد طعم ثمار الجنة .
The samʿiyyāt (matters heard from revelation). And it (the ḥawḍ) is a specific large body having wide sides, located upon the transformed earth (the white earth like silver). Whoever drinks from it will never thirst. This nation will come to it. And it has been reported that every prophet has a ḥawḍ which his nation comes to. From al-Ḥasan, raised (marfūʿ): 'Indeed, every prophet has a ḥawḍ, and he stands at his ḥawḍ with a staff in his hand calling those he knows from his nation. Lo! they boast as to which of them has more followers, and I hope to be the one with the most followers.' And in an athar (report): that his ḥawḍ is the widest of ḥawḍs and the most frequented. And the specification of our Prophet's ḥawḍ for mention is because it came in aḥādīth reaching the level of tawātur (mass transmission), unlike others which came in āḥād (solitary) reports. And his statement: 'as has come to us in transmission' means: the text that has reached us from that which is transmitted. For in the two Ṣaḥīḥs, from the ḥadīth of ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAmr ibn al-ʿĀṣ (may Allah be pleased with them both): 'My ḥawḍ is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its smell is sweeter than musk, its jugs are more numerous than the stars of the sky. Whoever drinks from it will never thirst.' And it has been reported with different estimates of directions. In a narration of Aḥmad: 'Indeed, the ḥawḍ is as between ʿAdan and ʿUmān' – that is about a month. And in a narration of the two Ṣaḥīḥs: '(It is) between Ṣanʿā' and al-Madīnah' – that is about two months. And in a narration: 'between Makkah and Aylah' – that is about a month. And in a narration of Ibn Mājah: 'between al-Madīnah and Bayt al-Maqdis' – which is like the previous one. So the Muṣṭafā (the Chosen One) spoke about the ḥadīth of the ḥawḍ multiple times and mentioned those different expressions. He addressed each group according to the direction they knew. And there is no contradiction in terms of estimating the distance as about a month in some narrations and about two months in others, because Allah (Exalted and High) favored him by enlarging it little by little. So he informed of the short distance first, then informed of the long distance. And reliance is on that which indicates the longest distance, as al-Nawawī indicated. And in what Allah revealed to ʿĪsā (peace be upon him) as a description of our Prophet: 'He has a ḥawḍ further than from Makkah to the rising place of the sun, in it are vessels like the number of the stars of the sky, and it has the color of every drink of Paradise and the taste of every fruit of Paradise.' And his statement in this narration 'like the number of the stars of the sky' does not contradict his statement in the previous narration 'more than the stars of the sky' because it is possible that he first informed that it is like, then secondly informed that it is more. And the meaning of 'it has the color of every drink of Paradise' is that some of it is red, some of it is white, and so on. And the meaning of 'it has the taste of every fruit of Paradise' is that it has the taste of peach, banana, apricot, and others. So whoever drinks from it finds the taste of the fruits of Paradise.

The Location of the Prophet's Basin: Opinions and Ruling
The author discusses differing opinions on the location of the Basin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing scholarly opinions on the location of the Prophet's Basin and why only belief in its existence is obligatory, not the exact location.

Core Idea
Only the existence of the Basin is obligatory to believe; its location is not required.

In the section on samiyyat (audible matters), the author addresses the Prophet's Basin (al-hawd). Though scholars have debated its exact location—whether before or after the Sirat—the author emphasizes that only the belief in its existence is essential. This lesson walks through the opinions and the final ruling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice how the author presents multiple views before giving the ruling.
The passage begins with 'السمعيات' and ends with the conclusion.
2
Identify the three opinions
List the three opinions: (1) before the Sirat, (2) after the Sirat, (3) two Basins. Note the supporters mentioned (majority, al-Qurtubi, etc.).
Each opinion is introduced with 'فقيل' or 'وقيل'.
3
Examine the arguments and rebuttals
For each opinion, the author gives a reason. For the second opinion, an objection and answer are provided. Understand the logic behind each.
The objection about the Basin being unnecessary near Paradise is answered with the Station of Retribution.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author states that none of these views are obligatory to believe; only the existence of the Basin is required. Ignorance of its location does no harm.
This is the key takeaway: freedom from unnecessary theological speculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمعيات
واختلف في محله :
فقيل : قبل الصراط، وهو قول الجمهور وصححه بعضهم؛ لأن الناس يخرجون من قبورهم عطاشاً فيردون الحوض للشرب منه .
وقيل : بعده وصححه بعضهم؛ لأنه ينصب فيه الماء من الكوثر؛ وهو النهر الذي في داخل الجنة، فيكون الحوض بعد الصراط بجانب الجنة ولو كان قبله لحالت النار بينه وبين الماء الذي ينصب فيه من الكوثر، وأورد عليه أن الحوض إذا كان عند الجنة لم يُحتج للشرب منه ، وأجيب بأنهم يحبسون هناك لأجل المظالم التي بينهم حتى يتحللوا منها، وهو المسمى بموقف القصاص.
وقيل : له حوضان يجب حوض قبل الصراط، وحوض بعده وصححه القرطبي، وهذا كله لا اعتقاده، وإنما يجب اعتقاد أنه له حوض ، ولا يضرُّ الجهل بكونه قبل الصراط أو بعده .
The auditory matters. And there is disagreement about its location: It is said: before the Sirat, and it is the saying of the majority and some authenticated it; because people come out of their graves thirsty so they go to the Basin to drink from it. And it is said: after it, and some authenticated it; because water flows into it from al-Kawthar, which is the river inside Paradise, so the Basin is after the Sirat beside Paradise; and if it were before it, the Fire would come between it and the water that flows into it from al-Kawthar. And an objection was raised against it that if the Basin is at Paradise, there is no need to drink from it. And it was answered that they are detained there for the injustices among them until they are released from them, and that is called the Station of Retribution. And it is said: he has two Basins, it is necessary a Basin before the Sirat and a Basin after it, and al-Qurtubi authenticated it. And all of this is not to be believed, but rather it is obligatory to believe that he has a Basin, and ignorance of whether it is before the Sirat or after it does no harm.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage discusses the location of the Prophet's Basin (al-hawd). The author presents three opinions: some say it is before the Sirat (the bridge over Hell), some after it, and a third opinion says there are two Basins—one before and one after. For each, he gives arguments and addresses a counterargument. He concludes that it is not obligatory to know the exact location; one must only believe that the Prophet has a Basin. Ignorance of its location does not harm one's faith.

Key Terms
الحوض
الصراط
الكوثر
موقف القصاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think it is necessary to know the exact location of the Prophet's Basin (e.g., before or after the Sirat) for correct faith.
Correction: The author clarifies that only belief in the existence of the Basin is obligatory. The location is a matter of scholarly discussion and ignorance of it does not harm one's faith.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding the location of the Prophet's Basin according to the author?
A) It is obligatory to know that it is before the Sirat.
B) It is obligatory to know that it is after the Sirat.
C) It is obligatory to believe that the Prophet has a Basin, but knowledge of its exact location is not required.
D) It is not obligatory to believe in the Basin at all.

Key Takeaway
It is obligatory to believe that the Prophet has a Basin, but not to know its exact location; ignorance of that detail does not harm.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that knowing the exact location of the Prophet's Basin is not required – only belief in its existence. Are there other details in your faith that you have turned into litmus tests for belief, while neglecting the core obligations that Allah and His Messenger actually commanded? Will you spend time today reviewing your priorities in what you insist upon in matters of unseen?
?
If you were to stand at the Prophet's Basin tomorrow, would you recognize your thirst for it? Or have you become so comfortable with the world that the thought of drinking from his hand no longer stirs your heart? What specific change can you make this week to revive that longing?
?
The passage mentions that the Basin is not just for quenching thirst but also for a station of retribution – where injustices are settled before entering Paradise. Is there someone you have wronged and have not sought forgiveness from? Will you take one concrete step today to settle that matter before you face that station?

Who Drinks from the Basin and the Covenant
The author explains who drinks from the Basin and the covenant's meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories of people who drink from the Prophet's Basin and the meaning of fulfilling the primordial covenant.

Core Idea
The covenant from Adam's loins determines who drinks from the Basin.

This lesson explores the author's explanation of the line 'A people will attain drink from it, those who fulfilled their covenant.' The passage describes different types of drinkers and the role of Muslim children, and it connects the covenant to the primordial testament of tawhid. Understanding this helps clarify the basis for entering the Prophet's Basin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's words settle before interpreting.
The passage is from Tuhfat al-Murid on Jawharat al-Tawhid.
2
Identify the categories of drinkers
Notice the three types of drinkers mentioned (to quench thirst, for pleasure, to hasten delight) and the description of Muslim children serving their parents.
The author includes both males and females in each group.
3
Understand the covenant and the hadith clarification
Focus on the definition of the covenant as the pact from Adam's loins and the author's note that although the description seems universal, hadiths specify only this nation comes to the Prophet's Basin.
The first to say 'Yes' was the Prophet Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : يَنالُ شُرْباً مِنْهُ أَقْوَامٌ) أي : يتعاطى الشرب من ذلك الحوض أقوام، والمراد بهم ما يشمل الذكور والإناث، وأحوالهم في الشرب مختلفة :
فمنهم من يشربُ لدفع العطش، ومنهم من يشرب للتلذذ، ومنهم من يشرب لتعجيل المسرَّةِ، وأطفال المسلمين ذكورهم وإناثهم حول الحوض وعليهم أقبية الديباج ومناديل من نورٍ، وبأيديهم أباريق الفضة وأقداح الذهب، يسقون آباءهم وأمهاتهم، إلا من سخط في فقدهم فلا يؤذن لهم أن يُسقوه .
وقوله : (وَفَوْا بِعَهْدِهِمْ) وصفٌ لأقوام أي وفوا الله تعالى بعهدهم؛ وهو الميثاق الذي أخذه عليهم حين أخرجهم من ظهر آدم عليه السلام: وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَتِكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۲] أي: أنت ربُّنا، وأول من قال: بلى: النبي . ومعنى وفائهم بعهدهم : أنهم لم يغيروه ولم يبدلوه حتى ماتوا ، وهذا الوصف وإن شمل جميع مؤمني الأمم السابقة لكنه خلاف ظاهر الأحاديث؛ من أنه لا يرده إلا مؤمنو هذه الأمة؛ لأنَّ كلَّ أمةٍ إنما ترد حوض نبيها .
His saying: 'A people will attain drink from it' means: a people will take drink from that Basin, and by them is meant what includes males and females, and their states in drinking are different: among them are those who drink to quench thirst, among them are those who drink for pleasure, and among them are those who drink to hasten delight. And the Muslim children, males and females, are around the Basin, upon them are brocade cloaks and handkerchiefs of light, and in their hands are silver ewers and gold cups, giving drink to their fathers and mothers, except for those who are displeased by their loss, so they are not permitted to give him drink. And his saying: 'and they fulfilled their covenant' is a description of a people, i.e., they fulfilled the covenant of Allah the Exalted; it is the pact that He took from them when He brought them out from the loins of Adam (peace be upon him): 'And He made them testify upon themselves, "Am I not your Lord?" They said, "Yes."' [al-A'raf 7:172] i.e., You are our Lord, and the first to say 'Yes' was the Prophet. And the meaning of their fulfilling their covenant is that they did not change it nor alter it until they died. And this description, although it includes all believers of previous nations, contradicts the apparent meaning of the hadiths, that only the believers of this nation will come to it, because every nation only comes to the Basin of its Prophet.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage explains the line 'A people will attain drink from it, those who fulfilled their covenant.' The author first describes the various groups who drink from the Basin: some drink to quench thirst, some for pleasure, some for delight. He also mentions that Muslim children will be present around the Basin, serving their parents drinks, except for those parents who were displeased by their children's loss. Then he explains the meaning of 'fulfilled their covenant': it refers to the primordial covenant taken from humanity in the loins of Adam, where they testified that Allah is their Lord. The first to say 'Yes' was the Prophet Muhammad. The author notes that although this description could apply to believers of all nations, the hadiths indicate that it is specifically the believers of this nation who will come to the Prophet's Basin, since every nation comes to the Basin of its own Prophet.

Key Terms
الشرب
الميثاق
العهد
أطفال المسلمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The covenant mentioned here is simply fulfilling religious duties like prayer and fasting.
Correction: The author explicitly defines the covenant as the primordial pact from Adam's loins where humanity testified that Allah is their Lord, and the first to say 'Yes' was the Prophet Muhammad.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what condition must someone meet to drink from the Prophet's Basin?
A) They must be a Muslim who never sinned.
B) They must have fulfilled the covenant they made with Allah from the time of Adam.
C) They must be from the Prophet's own tribe.
D) They must have performed many good deeds.

Key Takeaway
Those who fulfill the primordial covenant of tawhid are the ones who will drink from the Prophet's Basin, particularly the believers of this nation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have taken the covenant of 'Am I not your Lord?' and said 'Yes.' Have you altered that testimony in any part of your life? What would it take for you to die without having changed it?
?
Imagine seeing your child at the Basin, ready to serve you. If you are displeased with the loss of that child, you will be deprived. Are you truly patient with Allah's decree, or is there resentment in your heart? How will you work on that patience today?
?
The different motives for drinking—quenching thirst, pleasure, delight—which one drives your pursuit of the Prophet's Basin? Is your desire for the afterlife merely to escape punishment, or do you genuinely long for the pleasure of being near the Prophet? What step will you take to purify your intention?

The Two Types of Those Driven Away from the Basin
Classification of those driven away from the Basin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between disbelievers and sinful believers regarding the Basin and the role of Allah's will.

Core Idea
Some are driven away forever, others as punishment then allowed to drink.

The author clarifies a common misunderstanding: not all who are driven away from the Basin are permanently denied. He divides the driven away into two categories based on whether they are disbelievers or sinful believers, with the latter being subject to Allah's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Pay attention to the list of groups and the final classification.
The Arabic has an incomplete phrase marked with [؟]; this does not affect the main classification.
2
Identify the two categories
Notice that the author first lists various groups (apostates, innovators, etc.) and then narrows down to two categories: the disbelievers (driven away permanently) and the sinful believers (driven away as punishment but will eventually drink).
3
Understand the role of Allah's will
The passage states that for those who change by sins (not apostasy), their fate is subject to Allah's will: He may pardon or punish. This is separate from the final classification of the Basin.
The classification of the Basin concerns only the drink, not the ultimate fate in the Fire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَقُلْ : يُذَادُ مَنْ طَغَوْا) أي : وقُلْ قولاً باطنيًّا؛ وهو الاعتقاد يُطرد عنه أقوام ظلموا أنفسهم بأن غيّروا وبدَّلوا عهدهم الذي أخذه الله عليهم، فالمرتد من المطرودين، ومن أحدث في الدين ما لا يرضاه الله تعالى، ومن خالف جماعة المسلمين؛ كالخوارج والروافض والمعتزلة على اختلاف فرقهم، والظلمة الجائرون، والمعلنُ بالكبائر المستختُ بالمعاصي، وأهل الزيغ والبدع، لكن المبدل بالارتداد النار، والمُبدل بالمعاصي في المشيئة، فإن شاء الله عفا عنه، وإن شاء مخلد في [؟]. وظاهرُ ذلك أن جميع من ذكر لا يشرب منه أبداً، والذي عليه المحققون أن المطرودين عن الحوض قسمان :
قسم يُطرد حرماناً ؛ وهم الكفار فلا يشربون منه أبداً، وقسم يُطرد عقوبة له ثم يشربُ ؛ وهم عصاة المؤمنين فيشربون قبل دخولهم النار على الصحيح
His saying: 'and say: driven away are those who transgressed' means: and say a hidden saying, which is the belief, that a people who wronged themselves are driven away from him, because they changed and altered their covenant that Allah took from them. So the apostate is among the driven away, and whoever innovates in the religion what Allah does not approve, and whoever opposes the community of Muslims, like the Kharijites, the Rawafid, and the Mu'tazilites (with their different sects), and the unjust oppressors, and those who openly commit major sins and are disrespectful of sins, and the people of deviation and innovation. However, one who changes by apostasy (is destined for) the Fire, and one who changes by sins is subject to (Allah's) will: if Allah wills, He pardons him, and if He wills, He [punishes him?] eternally [؟]. And the apparent meaning of that is that all those mentioned will never drink from it. And what the verifiers hold is that the driven away from the Basin are of two types: a type driven away as deprivation, and they are the disbelievers, so they never drink from it; and a type driven away as punishment and then they drink, and they are the sinful believers, so they drink before their entry into the Fire, according to the correct opinion.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the verse, focusing on those who are driven away ('yudhadu man taghaw'). The author explains that the driven away are those who wronged themselves by changing the covenant. He lists categories: apostates, innovators, those who oppose the Muslim community (Kharijites, Rawafid, Mu'tazilites), tyrants, open sinners, and deviants. He distinguishes between those who changed by apostasy (destined for the Fire) and those who changed by sins (under Allah's will). Then he clarifies two categories of the driven away: disbelievers (permanently denied drink) and sinful believers (driven away as punishment but will eventually drink before entering the Fire).

Misconception: All who are driven away from the Basin never drink.
Correction: The author clarifies that only disbelievers are permanently denied; sinful believers are driven away as punishment but will eventually drink.

Checkpoint

A) They will never drink from it.
B) They are driven away permanently and then drink after entering Hell.

D) They are driven away only if they are apostates.

Key Takeaway
The Basin's driven away include both those permanently denied (disbelievers) and those temporarily punished (sinful believers) who will eventually drink.

?

The Obligation of Believing in the Prophet's Intercession
Declaration of obligation and definition of shafa'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of shafa'a and why believing in the Prophet's intercession is obligatory according to Sunni creed.

Core Idea
Intercession is a settled reality, not a human favor — it is Allah's pardon.

This lesson introduces a new section on sam'iyyat (matters of hearing) — the obligation to believe in the Prophet's intercession. The author clarifies the linguistic and technical meaning of shafa'a and distinguishes between the intercessor and the one who is interceded for. It also explains that ultimate intercession belongs to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation carefully. Let the author's own terms come through before interpreting.
Notice the use of the term 'mushaffa'' with different vowel markings.
2
Understand the term 'al-mushaffa''
The author explains that 'al-mushaffa'' (with fatha) is the one whose intercession is accepted (the Prophet). The one with kasra is the one who accepts intercession. Grasp this distinction.
This is a technical point that affects the understanding of who does what.
3
Grasp the definitions of shafa'a
Learn the linguistic and terminological definitions. Then understand 'shafa'at al-Mawla' as Allah's pardon — this is the ultimate intercession.
The Prophet's intercession is a means, but Allah's 'intercession' is His own attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَوَاجِبٌ شَفَاعَةُ المُشَفَّعِ مُحَمَّدٍ مُقَدَّماً لا تَمْنَعِ
قوله : (وَوَاجِبٌ شَفَاعَةُ المُشَفّع) أي : وواجب سمعاً عند أهل الحق)، شفاعة المشفّع، بفتح الفاء؛ وهو الذي تُقبل شفاعته وأما بكسرها فهو الذي يقبلُ شفاعة غيره .
والشفاعة لغةٌ : الوسيلة والطلب. وعرفاً سؤال الخير من الغير للغير. وشفاعةُ المولى (۲) : عبارةٌ عن عفوه ؛ فإنه تعالى يشفع فيمن قال : لا إله إلا الله، وأثبت الرسالة للرسول الذي أُرسل إليه، ولم يعمل خيراً قط، فيتفضل الله تعالى عليه بعدم دخوله النار بلا شفاعة أحدٍ .
And obligatory is the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted, Muhammad, advanced, do not prevent. His saying: 'and obligatory is the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted' means: it is obligatory (sam'an, by audition) according to the people of truth, the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted (with fatha on the fa'), and he is the one whose intercession is accepted; as for with kasra, he is the one who accepts the intercession of another. And intercession (shafa'a) in language is: the means and the request. And in technical terminology: asking for good from someone for someone else. And the intercession of the Master (al-Mawla) is an expression of His pardon; for He the Exalted intercedes for the one who says 'There is no god but Allah' and affirms the message for the messenger who was sent to him, and has not done any good whatsoever, so Allah the Exalted grants him favor by not entering the Fire without any intercession of anyone.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage introduces a new topic: the obligation of believing in the Prophet's intercession. The author states that it is obligatory (sam'an, by audition) to believe that the Prophet Muhammad's intercession will be accepted. He clarifies the term 'al-mushaffa'': with fatha on the fa', it means the one whose intercession is accepted (i.e., the Prophet); with kasra, it means the one who accepts intercession. Then he defines shafa'a linguistically and technically. He also mentions 'shafa'at al-Mawla' (the intercession of the Lord), which is an expression for Allah's pardon: He will forgive those who professed tawhid even if they did no good deeds, without any intercessor. This passage emphasizes the importance of affirming the Prophet's intercession as part of Sunni creed.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
المشفع
المولى
سمعاً
أهل الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that the Prophet's intercession is independent of Allah's will or that it is a kind of bargaining.
Correction: The Prophet's intercession is a means granted by Allah, and the true 'intercession' is Allah's pardon. The passage clarifies that Allah 'intercedes' (i.e., forgives) directly for those who have tawhid, without any intermediary, showing that all intercession is subject to His will.

Checkpoint
How does the author define 'al-mushaffa'' (with fatha on the fa')?
A) The one who accepts intercession from others.
B) The one whose intercession is accepted.
C) The intercession itself.
D) The one who intercedes for others.

Key Takeaway
Believing in the Prophet's intercession is obligatory, but it is ultimately an expression of Allah's pardon for those who affirm tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely trust in Allah's pardon alone, or do you subconsciously rely on the Prophet's intercession as a 'safety net' that allows you to neglect your duties? If you knew that only your tawhid and sincerity would matter, how would you change your daily life?
?
The passage describes a person who said 'La ilaha illallah' but did no good. If you were to die tonight, would your shahada be enough? What does your answer reveal about your heart's reliance on Allah's mercy versus your own deeds?
?
When you ask for forgiveness, do you turn directly to Allah, or do you sometimes think of the Prophet as an intermediary who must plead for you? How does this lesson challenge your understanding of tawhid in your personal supplications?

The Two Categories of Those Repelled from the Prophet's Fountain
Explains who is repelled from the Hawd and divides them into two categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the scholars divide those repelled from the Prophet's Hawd into two categories: disbelievers who never drink, and sinful believers who are punished but eventually drink.

Core Idea
Not all who are repelled are equal: disbelievers are permanently deprived, sinners are temporarily punished.

In this passage, the author explains the types of people who are repelled from the Prophet's fountain (al-hawḍ). While the apparent meaning suggests all listed sinners never drink, the verified scholars (al-muḥaqqiqūn) refine this into two distinct categories. This lesson will clarify that distinction and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to understand the author's listing of repelled groups.
2
Identify the two categories
Focus on the final part where the scholars divide the repelled into two types: deprivation vs punishment.
Notice the key terms: حرماناً and عقوبة.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this distinction matters for understanding Allah's mercy and justice.
The sinful believers still receive the Prophet's intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَقُلْ : يُذَادُ مَنْ طَغَوْا) أي : وقُلْ قولاً باطنيًّا؛ وهو الاعتقاد يُطرد عنه أقوام ظلموا أنفسهم بأن غيّروا وبدَّلوا عهدهم الذي أخذه الله عليهم، فالمرتد من المطرودين، ومن أحدث في الدين ما لا يرضاه الله تعالى، ومن خالف جماعة المسلمين؛ كالخوارج والروافض والمعتزلة على اختلاف فرقهم، والظلمة الجائرون، والمعلنُ بالكبائر المستختُ بالمعاصي، وأهل الزيغ والبدع، لكن المبدل بالارتداد النار، والمُبدل بالمعاصي في المشيئة، فإن شاء الله عفا عنه، وإن شاء عاقبه . في وظاهرُ ذلك أن جميع من ذكر لا يشرب منه أبداً، والذي عليه المحققون أن المطرودين عن الحوض قسمان : قسم يُطرد حرماناً ؛ وهم الكفار فلا يشربون منه أبداً، وقسم يُطرد عقوبة له ثم يشربُ ؛ وهم عصاة المؤمنين فيشربون قبل دخولهم النار على الصحيح
(He said: 'And say: Those who transgress are repelled.') That is: And say an inward saying, which is belief: that are repelled from him people who wronged themselves by changing and altering the covenant that Allah took from them. Thus the apostate is among the repelled, and whoever innovates in religion that which Allah does not approve, and whoever opposes the community of Muslims, such as the Khawarij, the Rawafid, and the Mu'tazila with their differing sects, and the unjust oppressors, and those who openly commit major sins and persist in disobediences, and the people of deviation and innovation. But the one who changes by apostasy [is subject to] the Fire, and the one who changes by sins is under the will; if Allah wills, He forgives him, and if He wills, He punishes him. And the apparent meaning of that is that all those mentioned never drink from it. But what the scholars have affirmed is that those repelled from the Hawd are of two types: a type that is repelled as a deprivation, and they are the disbelievers, so they never drink from it; and a type that is repelled as a punishment, then drinks, and they are the sinful believers, so they drink before entering the Fire, according to the sound opinion.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage explains the meaning of the Qur'anic phrase 'And say: Those who transgress are repelled' in the context of the Prophet's fountain (al-ḥawḍ). First, it clarifies that this is an inward saying—a belief—that certain people are repelled from the fountain. These include: apostates, those who innovate in religion, those who oppose the Muslim community (like the Khawarij, Rawafid, and Mu'tazila), unjust oppressors, open sinners, and people of deviation. The passage then distinguishes consequences: the apostate is destined for the Fire, while the sinner is subject to Allah's will—He may forgive or punish. After listing these groups, the author notes that the apparent meaning is that all such people never drink from the fountain. However, the verified scholars (al-muḥaqqiqūn) refine this into two categories: those repelled permanently as a deprivation (the disbelievers, who never drink), and those repelled temporarily as a punishment (the sinful believers, who eventually drink before entering the Fire). This clarifies that the fountain's exclusion is not absolute for all sinners.

Key Terms
يُذَاد
الحوض
المطرودون
الكفار
عصاة المؤمنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All who are repelled from the Hawd are permanently deprived and never drink.
Correction: The correct view distinguishes between disbelievers (permanent deprivation) and sinful believers (temporary punishment, then drink).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between the two types of people repelled from the Hawd?
A) Both are permanently deprived.
B) One type is permanently deprived (disbelievers), the other is temporarily punished then drinks (sinful believers).
C) Both will drink after punishment.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's fountain is a blessing for believers; even sinful believers will eventually drink after punishment, while disbelievers are forever deprived.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
You have learned that sinful believers will drink after punishment—but only if they are believers. Does your heart hold firm to faith despite your shortcomings, or are you sliding into disbelief? What is the one sin you need to repent from right now to secure your place at the Hawd?

Refuting the Mu'tazilah Denial of Intercession
Refutation of Mu'tazilah on intercession for major sinners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the Prophet's intercession for major sinners and how the Mu'tazilah deviation is refuted.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession benefits even major sinners; the hadith denying it is fabricated.

The Mu'tazilah limited the Prophet's intercession to those not deserving Hell, but Sunni scholars affirm intercession for major sinners both before and after entry into Hell. This passage from Tuhfat al-Murid explains the author's command not to prevent intercession and refutes the opposing view. It also addresses a fabricated hadith used to support the Mu'tazilah claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's discussion of intercession types and refutation come through.
Notice the phrase 'لا تمنع' and its explanation.
2
Identify the three types of intercession
The passage mentions three types: the great intercession, intercession for increasing ranks, and intercession for major sinners (to avoid or exit Hell). Note which the Mu'tazilah deny.
3
Understand the ruling on the fabricated hadith
The commentator states that the hadith 'My intercession will not reach people of major sins' is fabricated by consensus. If authentic, it would refer to apostates.
This directly refutes the Mu'tazilah proof.
4
Reflect on the footnote about Allah's mercy
The footnote explains that Allah's mercy is universal before judgment, but after entry into Paradise or Hell, mercy is specified for believers.
This supports the possibility of intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : لا تَمْنَع) أي: لا تعتقد امتناع شفاعته في أهل الكبائر وغيرهم لا قبل دخولهم النار ولا بعده، وقصد المصنف بذلك الردّ على المعتزلة، ومن وافقهم في إنكارهم شفاعته فيمن استحق النار ألا يدخلها، وفيمن دخلها أن يخرج منها . وأما الشفاعة العظمى فلا يُنكرونها، وكذا الشفاعة في زيادة الدرجات، وحديث: لا تنال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي موضوع باتفاق، وبتقدير صحته فهو محمول على من ارتد منهم
(1) رحمة الله تعالى في قوله : يَخْتَصُّ بِرَحْمَتِهِ مَن يَشَاءُ ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ١٠٥]، هذا الاختصاص واقع بعد ﴿ دخول الدارين فيختص برحمته المؤمنين، ويختص بغضبه الكافرين، أما قبل ذلك وَرَحْمَتِي وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ) [الأعراف: ١٥٦].
His saying: 'Do not prevent' i.e., do not believe in the impossibility of his intercession for the people of major sins and others, neither before their entry into the Fire nor after it, and the author's intent by that is the refutation of the Mu'tazilah, and those who agreed with them in their denial of his intercession for those who deserved the Fire from entering it, and for those who entered it from coming out of it. As for the great intercession, they do not deny it, and likewise the intercession for increasing ranks. And the hadith: 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins from my ummah' is fabricated by consensus, and if it were considered authentic, it is interpreted as referring to those who apostatized from among them.
(1) The mercy of Allah the Exalted in His saying: 'He specifies His mercy to whom He wills' [al-Baqarah:105]; this specification occurs after the entry into the two abodes, so He specifies with His mercy the believers, and specifies with His wrath the disbelievers. As for before that, 'And My mercy encompasses all things' [al-A'raf:156].
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of the Mu'tazilah and their allies who deny that the Prophet's intercession benefits those who commit major sins (kaba'ir). The commentator explains the author's phrase 'do not prevent' as a prohibition against believing that intercession is impossible (imtina') for such people, both before they enter the Fire (to prevent entry) and after they have entered (to bring them out). The Mu'tazilah, we are told, do not deny the great intercession (al-shafa'ah al-'uzma) or the intercession for increasing ranks, but they deny intercession for those who deserved the Fire. The commentator then addresses the hadith: 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins from my ummah' by stating that it is fabricated (mawdu') by consensus. If one were to assume its authenticity, it would be interpreted as referring to apostates (murtaddun), not to sinful believers. The footnote adds a theological note about Allah's mercy: His specification of mercy occurs after entry into the abodes (Paradise and Hell), whereas before that His mercy encompasses everything.

Key Terms

أهل الكبائر
الشفاعة العظمى
حديث موضوع
الردّ

Misconception: Some think that the Prophet's intercession does not benefit those who commit major sins, based on a hadith.
Correction: The hadith in question is fabricated by consensus. The Prophet's intercession includes major sinners, as affirmed by Sunni scholars.

The Benefit of Intercession: Answering an Objection
Commentator answers objection about intercession's benefit after punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why intercession after punishment is beneficial and how it relates to the concept of suspended decree.

Core Idea
Intercession after punishment reveals the intercessor's rank and clarifies divine decree.

Some have questioned the benefit of intercession after punishment has already occurred, arguing it serves no purpose. The commentator rebuts this by highlighting two key benefits: showing the intercessor's superiority and clarifying the suspended nature of God's decree. In this passage, we explore this subtle theological point.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note the structure: 'fain qīla' introduces the objection, and 'ujība' begins the answer.
This format is common in kalam texts.
2
Identify the two benefits
The answer provides two distinct benefits of intercession. Find them: one about the intercessor's superiority, the other about uncertainty without intercession.
3
Connect to suspended decree
The passage concludes by labeling this as an example of al-qaḍā' al-mu'allaq. Reflect on what that means: a decree conditional on causes.
This ties intercession to the broader kalam topic of divine decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لا فائدة في الشفاعة حينئذ . . أجيب بأن فائدتها إظهار مزية الشافع على غيره على أنه لولا الشفاعة لجوزنا البقاء وعدمه بحسب الظاهر لنا، وبالجملة فذلك من باب القضاء المعلق.
For if it is said: There is no benefit in intercession at that time. . It is answered: That its benefit is the manifestation of the superiority of the intercessor over others, and that were it not for intercession, we would have considered the possibility of remaining (in punishment) and not remaining according to what is apparent to us. In summary, that is from the category of suspended decree (al-qaḍā' al-mu'allaq).
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage presents an objection (qīla) and its answer (ujība). The objection claims that intercession after the punishment period has ended has no benefit, since the person is already out or already punished. The answer provides two points: (1) the benefit is to show the superiority (maziyyah) of the intercessor over others; (2) without intercession, we would consider the possibility of the person remaining in punishment indefinitely based on our apparent understanding. In other words, intercession ensures the removal or mitigation of punishment. The conclusion describes this as an example of suspended decree (al-qaḍā' al-mu'allaq), meaning a decree contingent on conditions.

Key Terms
القضاء المعلق
مزية الشافع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession after punishment has no benefit.
Correction: The answer shows two benefits: manifesting the intercessor's superiority and clarifying the uncertainty of the duration of punishment without intercession.

Checkpoint

A) It reduces the severity of punishment
B) It shows the superiority of the intercessor and clarifies that without it, one would not know if punishment continues
C) It allows the intercessor to enter Paradise
D) It cancels the punishment entirely

Key Takeaway
Intercession after punishment benefits by displaying the intercessor's honor and by removing uncertainty about the punishment's duration, illustrating the category of suspended decree.

Types of the Prophet's Intercession and Refutation of Mu'tazila
The author lists kinds of shafa'ah and denies Mu'tazila's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the types of the Prophet's intercession and the refutation of the Mu'tazila's denial of intercession for major sinners.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession includes removing monotheists from the Fire, increasing degrees in Paradise, and more, even for major sinners.

This passage from the Jawharah commentary enumerates the kinds of the Prophet's intercession (shafa'ah) and then addresses a key sectarian dispute. The author firmly refutes the Mu'tazila who deny that the Prophet can intercede for those who commit major sins, and he dismisses a contradictory hadith as fabricated. Let's examine the text to understand both the types of intercession and the theological defense.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall meaning.
2
Identify the types of intercession
Look for the explicit types listed: removal from the Fire, increase in degrees, and other kinds mentioned by al-Suyuti.
Notice the phrase 'منها' which indicates enumeration.
3
Understand the author's comment on 'la tamna'
The phrase means 'do not prevent' or 'do not believe it is impossible.' The author clarifies it negates any denial of intercession for major sinners, before or after entering the Fire.
This is a direct refutation of the Mu'tazila.
4
Recognize the Mu'tazila's position
The Mu'tazila deny intercession for those who deserve the Fire, but they accept the greater intercession (al-shafa'ah al-uzma) and intercession for increasing degrees.
Know that they are not entirely denying all intercession.
5
Analyze the fabricated hadith
The hadith 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins' is unanimously fabricated. If authentic, it would be interpreted as referring to apostates only.
This shows the importance of hadith criticism in theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها شفاعته في إخراج الموحدين من النار. وغيرها في زيادة الدرجات في الجنة لأهلها. ومنها شفاعته. ومنها غير ذلك كما ذكره السيوطي وغيره. قوله : لا تَمْنَع) أي: لا تعتقد امتناع شفاعته في أهل الكبائر وغيرهم لا قبل دخولهم النار ولا بعده، وقصد المصنف بذلك الردّ على المعتزلة، ومن وافقهم في إنكارهم شفاعته فيمن استحق النار ألا يدخلها، وفيمن دخلها أن يخرج منها . وأما الشفاعة العظمى فلا يُنكرونها، وكذا الشفاعة في زيادة الدرجات، وحديث: لا تنال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي موضوع باتفاق، وبتقدير صحته فهو محمول على من ارتد منهم
And among them is his intercession in removing the monotheists from the Fire. And others in increasing degrees in Paradise for its inhabitants. And among them is his intercession. And among them is other than that as al-Suyuti and others mentioned. His statement: 'Do not prevent' means: do not believe in the impossibility of his intercession for the people of major sins and others, neither before their entering the Fire nor after, and the author's intent by that is the refutation of the Mu'tazila and those who agreed with them in their denial of his intercession for those who deserve the Fire not to enter it, and for those who entered it to exit from it. As for the greater intercession, they do not deny it, and likewise the intercession in increasing degrees. And the hadith: 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins from my ummah' is fabricated by agreement, and if it were authentic, it would be interpreted as referring to those who apostatized from them.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage begins by enumerating the kinds of the Prophet's intercession: intercession to remove monotheists from the Fire, intercession to increase degrees in Paradise, and other kinds mentioned by scholars like al-Suyuti. Then the author comments on the line 'Do not prevent' (la tamna'), explaining that it means we must not believe that intercession is impossible for major sinners, whether before or after entering the Fire. The author's aim is to refute the Mu'tazila and their followers, who deny that the Prophet can intercede for those who deserve the Fire to prevent their entry, or to bring them out if they have entered. However, the Mu'tazila do not deny the greater intercession (al-shafa'ah al-uzma) nor intercession for increasing degrees. The author then mentions that the hadith 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins from my ummah' is unanimously fabricated, and if it were authentic, it would be interpreted as referring to those who apostatized from the ummah (i.e., became apostates).

Key Takeaway

Intercession of the Righteous and the Objection Answered
The author affirms intercession and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that intercession is not limited to the Prophet but includes other righteous figures, and you will learn how the objection about its benefit is resolved.

Core Idea
Intercession manifests the merit of the intercessor and is a matter of suspended decree.

This lesson continues the topic of intercession by affirming that many righteous figures intercede on behalf of sinners. The author also addresses a potential objection: if intercession occurs only after judgment, what benefit does it have? The answer reveals the wisdom behind intercession and clarifies its role in Allah’s decree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the righteous figures who intercede
Read the passage and list the categories of people mentioned as intercessors besides the Prophet. Notice the order of angels specifically.
The list includes prophets, messengers, angels, companions, martyrs, scholars, and saints.
2
Note the condition for intercession
The text states that none intercedes until after the period of accountability ends. Understand what this condition implies.
This ensures that intercession is not a mere intervention against justice.
3
Understand the objection and answer
The objection claims that if intercession occurs after judgment, it has no benefit. Find how the author responds and explain the benefit he mentions.
The benefit is to show the merit of the intercessor and resolve ambiguity about the decree.
4
Connect to suspended decree
The author concludes that this is a case of 'suspended decree'. Reflect on how this concept reconciles divine decree with human actions and intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغَيْرُهُ مِنْ مُرْتَضَى الأَخْيَارِ يَشْفَعْ كَمَا قَدْ جاءَ فِي الأَخْبَارِ قوله : وغَيْرُهُ مِنْ مُرْتَضَى الأَخْيارِ يَشْفَعُ بسكون العين للوزن؛ أي: وغيره ممن ارتضاه الله تعالى من الأخيار ؛ كالأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة والصحابة والشهداء والعلماء العاملين والأولياء يشفعُ في أرباب الكبائر على قدر مقامه عند الله تعالى وشفاعة الملائكة على الترتيب ؛ فأولهم في الشفاعة جبريلُ، وآخرهم فيها التسعة عشر التي على النار . وقوله : كَمَا قَدْ جاءَ في الأَخْبَارِ) أي : للنص الذي قد جاء في الأخبار الدالَّةِ على ذلك، كما أجمع عليه أهل السنة، ولا يشفع أحد ممن ذُكر إلا بعد انتهاء مُدَّة المؤاخذة. فإن قيل : لا فائدة في الشفاعة حينئذ . . أجيب بأن فائدتها إظهار مزية الشافع على غيره على أنه لولا الشفاعة لجوزنا البقاء وعدمه بحسب الظاهر لنا، وبالجملة فذلك من باب القضاء المعلق.
And other than him from the chosen righteous ones intercede, as has come in the reports. His statement: 'And other than him from the chosen righteous ones intercede' with sukun on the 'ayn for the meter; meaning: and other than him from those whom Allah has chosen from the righteous—such as the prophets, messengers, angels, companions, martyrs, acting scholars, and saints—intercede for the people of major sins according to his rank with Allah, and the intercession of the angels is in order; the first of them in intercession is Jibril, and the last of them are the nineteen over the Fire. And his statement: 'As has come in the reports' means: according to the text that has come in the reports indicating that, as the Ahl al-Sunnah have agreed upon, and none of those mentioned intercedes except after the period of accountability ends. If it is said: There is no benefit in intercession then. The answer: Its benefit is to show the merit of the intercessor over others, and that were it not for intercession, we would have considered both permanence and non-permanence as possible according to our apparent view, and in short, that is of the type of suspended decree.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage explains the line of the poem 'And other than him from the chosen righteous ones intercede.' The author clarifies that besides the Prophet, others whom Allah has chosen—such as prophets, messengers, angels, companions, martyrs, acting scholars, and saints—also intercede for people of major sins, each according to his rank. The intercession of angels has an order: first Jibril, and last are the nineteen angels over the Fire. This is based on texts from the reports and the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah. An important condition is that none of them intercedes until after the period of accountability (mu'akhadhah) ends. Then an objection is raised: if intercession only occurs after accountability, what benefit does it have? The objection implies that since everyone has already been judged, intercession seems pointless. The answer is that the benefit is to manifest the superiority (maziyyah) of the intercessor over others. Moreover, without intercession, we would have considered both permanence and non-permanence of punishment as possible from our apparent perspective; intercession removes that ambiguity. In summary, this is a case of 'suspended decree' (al-qada' al-mu'allaq)—a decree that depends on conditions.

Key Terms
مرتضى الأخيار
الملائكة
القضاء المعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Intercession has no benefit if it occurs after judgment.
Correction: The benefit is to show the intercessor's rank and resolve ambiguity about the decree; it is part of Allah's suspended decree.

B) Israfil
C) Jibril
D) The nineteen over the Fire

Key Takeaway
